٢٦ ) قالت نظرية القرآن في المعرفة ان الجنون هو سيطرة الشياطين على النفس مما يؤدي الى انهيار نظام البصائر و لم تتطرق نظريات الفلاسفة لهذا الموضوع البتة . لقد تغافل الفلاسفة عن هذا الموضوع المعرفي المهم وأحالوه الى علم النفس الذي هرب من معالجته أو تفسيره وحول الموضوع مرة اخرى الى الطب النفسي الذي اكتفى بوضع العلاجات المسكنة أو المخدرة.
٢٧ ) اللغة في نظريات الفلاسفة تتكون من خلال الخبرة والتدريب والحاجة أما في نظرية القرآن فان مفرداتها الاساسية الاولى هي الهام من الله (وعلم آدم الاسماء كلها) (علمه البيان)
٢٨ ) اختلف القرآن الكريم حول موضوع الرؤيا المنامية مع نظريات الفلاسفة ففي حين قال القرآن انها مصدر مهم من مصادر المعرفة قالت نظريات الفلاسفة ان الرؤيا المنامية هي تجليات نفسية لاقيمة لها وقال بعضهم ان الرؤيا عبارة عن اضطرابات نفسية ولابد من تسجيل اعتراف دیکارت بدور الرؤيا المنامية في الهامه علم الهندسة التحليلية ولكن هذا الاعتراف لم تكن غايته الاشارة العلمية المنهجية الرصينة بكون الرؤيا المنامية مصدرا للمعرفة بل كانت من باب تسجيل الحكاية الغريبة العجيبة مما لا يعطي لاعتراف ديكارت هذا اية قيمة بل نسجل هذه الرؤيا كنقطة خلل في تفكيره وليس العكس.
٢٩ ) قالت نظرية القرآن الكريم ان المعرفة اليقينية ممكنة للبشر ممن طهرت قلوبهم وصفت اذهانهم وقاموا بالرياضات الروحية والمجاهدات النفسية حيث سترتفع الحجب عن هؤلاء فيعرفون اسرار الكون والعالم كمن يرى في المرآة فيرى ما يحتاج او يريد من الماضي او الحاضر او المستقبل في حين وقفت نظريات الفلاسفة عند حدود الاستدلالات والبراهين العقلية. ويمكن استثناء النظرية الصوفية من هذه القاعدة مع اختلافها عن القرآن الكريم في الموارد والمقاصد .
٣٠ ) اختلف القرآن الكريم مع نظرية التحليل النفسي في تقدير قيمة الغريزة الجنسية ففي حين قال القرآن ان لهذه الغريزة اهمية بالغة في بعض قرارات النفس فتزيدها سلبا او ايجابا قالت نظرية التحليل النفسي ان الغريزة الجنسية هي الجوهر والاصل والمسبب للمعرفة .
٣١) الفيلسوف في نظرية المعرفة يريد ان يفهم العالم والعارف يريد ان يصل الى كنه وحقيقة الوجود ويتصل به ويشاهده .
(٣٢) الادوات التي يستخدمها الفيلسوف في حركته العقل والمنطق والاستدلال في حين ان العارف يضيف لها القلب والتصفية والتهذيب.
24) The Quranic theory dealt with moral values as fixed axioms and mental postulates, while most philosophical theories dealt with moral values as accidental results of knowledge. 25) The Quranic theory spoke about the inheritance of negative and positive traits, such as the inheritance of the bad side (as in the case of the Children of Israel) and the inheritance of the positive side (as in the inheritance of the family of Yasin), while philosophical theories of knowledge did not pay attention to this aspect at all. 26) The Quranic theory stated that there are destructive and evil elements that affect the decision made by humans, namely the devils, while philosophical theories considered matters of good and evil as relative issues that change according to temporal and spatial conditions. 26) The Quranic theory stated in knowledge that insanity is the domination of devils over the soul, leading to the collapse of the system of insight, and philosophical theories did not address this topic at all. Philosophers neglected this important epistemological topic and referred it to psychology, which avoided its treatment or interpretation, and turned it back to psychiatry, which sufficed with palliative or anesthetic treatments. 27) Language in philosophical theories is formed through experience, training, and need, while in the Quranic theory its primary basic vocabulary is inspiration from God (And He taught Adam all the names) (He taught him expression). 28) The Holy Quran differed with philosophical theories on the subject of dreams. While the Quran said they are an important source of knowledge, philosophical theories said that dreams are psychological manifestations of no value, and some said that dreams are psychological disturbances. Descartes' acknowledgment of the role of dreams in inspiring him with analytical geometry must be recorded, but this acknowledgment was not intended as a sound methodological scientific indication that dreams are a source of knowledge, but rather as a recording of a strange and wondrous story, which does not give Descartes' acknowledgment any value. Rather, we record this dream as a point of defect in his thinking, not the opposite. 29) The Holy Quranic theory said that certain knowledge is possible for humans whose hearts are purified, their minds clear, and who perform spiritual exercises and psychic struggles, so the veils will be lifted from them and they will know the secrets of the universe and the world like one who sees in a mirror and sees what he needs or wants from the past, present, or future, while philosophical theories stopped at rational inferences and proofs. The Sufi theory can be excepted from this rule, though it differs from the Holy Quran in resources and purposes. 30) The Holy Quran differed with the theory of psychoanalysis in estimating the value of the sexual instinct. While the Quran said that this instinct has great importance in some decisions of the soul, increasing it negatively or positively, the theory of psychoanalysis said that the sexual instinct is the essence, origin, and cause of knowledge. 31) The philosopher in the theory of knowledge wants to understand the world, while the gnostic wants to reach the essence and reality of existence, connect with it, and witness it. 32) The tools used by the philosopher in his movement are intellect, logic, and inference, while the gnostic adds to them the heart, purification, and discipline.

Commentary
This passage is a comparative enumeration by the author of ten points distinguishing the Quranic theory of knowledge from various philosophical theories. The author proceeds by stating each contrast directly. Point 24: The Quran treats moral values as fixed, axiomatic truths, whereas philosophy sees them as contingent byproducts of knowledge. Point 25: The Quran acknowledges hereditary transmission of both positive and negative traits (citing the Israelites and the family of Yasin), which philosophy ignores. Point 26 (first): The Quran affirms the existence of satanic influences on human decision-making, while philosophy relativizes good and evil to time and place. Point 26 (second): The Quran attributes insanity to demonic possession and collapse of insight, while philosophy relegates it to psychology and then to psychiatry, offering only palliative treatments. Point 27: Language, for philosophy, arises from experience, training, and need; for the Quran, it is divinely inspired, as in the verse 'And He taught Adam all the names' and 'He taught him expression.' Point 28: The Quran values dreams as a source of knowledge; philosophy dismisses them as valueless psychic phenomena. The author criticizes Descartes' acknowledgment of a dream inspiring his geometry as a mere curiosity, not a valid epistemological source. Point 29: Certain knowledge is attainable for those who purify heart and mind through spiritual discipline, leading to direct vision of past, present, and future; philosophy limits itself to rational proofs. The author notes an exception for Sufism but emphasizes its divergence from the Quran. Point 30: The Quran acknowledges the sexual instinct's influence on the soul positively or negatively; psychoanalysis treats it as the essence and origin of all knowledge. Point 31: The philosopher seeks to understand the world; the gnostic seeks to reach and witness the reality of existence. Point 32: The philosopher's tools are intellect, logic, and inference; the gnostic adds the heart, purification, and self-discipline.

The Path to Certain Knowledge: Purification vs Rational Proof
Author's contrast on certain knowledge and tools

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Quranic claim that certain knowledge (yaqin) requires spiritual purification, as opposed to pure rational inference, and identify the tools of the gnostic versus the philosopher.

Core Idea
Certain knowledge is not merely logical; it requires a purified heart.

The author presents a striking contrast: the Quran promises certain knowledge to those who purify themselves through spiritual exercises, while philosophy limits itself to rational proofs. The gnostic (arif) goes beyond the philosopher by using the heart, purification, and discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for certain knowledge in the Quranic view
Look for the phrases describing purification, spiritual struggles, and lifting of veils.
From point 29: 'whose hearts are purified, their minds clear, and who perform spiritual exercises and psychic struggles, so the veils will be lifted from them'
2
Contrast with the philosophical method
Philosophical theories stop at rational inferences and proofs; they do not incorporate purification.
Same point: 'philosophical theories stopped at rational inferences and proofs'
3
Compare the tools of philosopher and gnostic
Point 32 lists the philosopher's tools as intellect, logic, inference; the gnostic adds heart, purification, discipline.
Point 32: 'The tools used by the philosopher... are intellect, logic, and inference, while the gnostic adds to them the heart, purification, and discipline.'

Evil, Inheritance, and Mental Health in Quranic Epistemology
Author's contrasts on evil, inheritance, and insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Quranic claims about inherited traits, demonic influence, and the spiritual cause of insanity, and contrast them with philosophical silence or reduction.

Core Idea
The Quran provides a metaphysical explanation for moral and mental phenomena that philosophy and modern science miss.

The author brings up topics that philosophy either ignores or misattributes: the inheritance of character traits (good and bad), the role of devils in human decisions, and the demonic cause of insanity. These are essential to a complete theory of knowledge because they affect human perception and decision-making.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Quranic claims
Find in the passage: (1) inheritance of negative and positive traits, (2) influence of devils on decisions, (3) insanity as demonic domination.
Points 25 and 26 (both mentions) cover these.
2
Note how philosophy handles each
Philosophy ignores inheritance of traits, relativizes good/evil, and refers insanity to psychology/psychiatry without spiritual cause.
The passage says philosophy 'did not pay attention to this aspect at all' for inheritance, 'considered matters of good and evil as relative', and 'did not address this topic at all' for insanity.
3
Assess the epistemological significance
If devils influence decisions, then knowledge acquisition is not purely rational; external metaphysical factors matter.
This challenges the autonomy of human reason assumed by philosophy.

٢٤ ) تعاملت نظرية القرآن مع القيم الاخلاقية كمسلمات ثابتة وبدهيات عقلية في حين تعاملت اغلب نظريات الفلاسفة مع القيم الاخلاقية كنتائج عرضية للمعرفة .
٢٥ ) تحدثت نظرية القرآن عن توارث الصفات السلبية منها والايجابية کتوارث الجانب السيء ) كما هو حال بني اسرائيل ) وتوارث الجانب الايجابي ) كتوارث آل ياسين ( في حين لم تلتفت نظريات الفلاسفة في المعرفة لهذا الجانب مطلقا.
٢٦ ) قالت نظرية القرآن الكريم بوجود عناصر تخريب وشر تؤثر في القرار الذي يتخذه الانسان وهم الشياطين في حين عدت نظريات الفلاسفة موضوعات الخير والشر بكونها مسائل نسبية تتغير حسب الظروف الزمانية والمكانية.
٢٦ ) قالت نظرية القرآن في المعرفة ان الجنون هو سيطرة الشياطين على النفس مما يؤدي الى انهيار نظام البصائر و لم تتطرق نظريات الفلاسفة لهذا الموضوع البتة . لقد تغافل الفلاسفة عن هذا الموضوع المعرفي المهم وأحالوه الى علم النفس الذي هرب من معالجته أو تفسيره وحول الموضوع مرة اخرى الى الطب النفسي الذي اكتفى بوضع العلاجات المسكنة أو المخدرة.
٢٧ ) اللغة في نظريات الفلاسفة تتكون من خلال الخبرة والتدريب والحاجة أما في نظرية القرآن فان مفرداتها الاساسية الاولى هي الهام من الله (وعلم آدم الاسماء كلها) (علمه البيان)
٢٨ ) اختلف القرآن الكريم حول موضوع الرؤيا المنامية مع نظريات الفلاسفة ففي حين قال القرآن انها مصدر مهم من مصادر المعرفة قالت نظريات الفلاسفة ان الرؤيا المنامية هي تجليات نفسية لاقيمة لها وقال بعضهم ان الرؤيا عبارة عن اضطرابات نفسية ولابد من تسجيل اعتراف دیکارت بدور الرؤيا المنامية في الهامه علم الهندسة التحليلية ولكن هذا الاعتراف لم تكن غايته الاشارة العلمية المنهجية الرصينة بكون الرؤيا المنامية مصدرا للمعرفة بل كانت من باب تسجيل الحكاية الغريبة العجيبة مما لا يعطي لاعتراف ديكارت هذا اية قيمة بل نسجل هذه الرؤيا كنقطة خلل في تفكيره وليس العكس.
٢٩ ) قالت نظرية القرآن الكريم ان المعرفة اليقينية ممكنة للبشر ممن طهرت قلوبهم وصفت اذهانهم وقاموا بالرياضات الروحية والمجاهدات النفسية حيث سترتفع الحجب عن هؤلاء فيعرفون اسرار الكون والعالم كمن يرى في المرآة فيرى ما يحتاج او يريد من الماضي او الحاضر او المستقبل في حين وقفت نظريات الفلاسفة عند حدود الاستدلالات والبراهين العقلية. ويمكن استثناء النظرية الصوفية من هذه القاعدة مع اختلافها عن القرآن الكريم في الموارد والمقاصد .
٣٠ ) اختلف القرآن الكريم مع نظرية التحليل النفسي في تقدير قيمة الغريزة الجنسية ففي حين قال القرآن ان لهذه الغريزة اهمية بالغة في بعض قرارات النفس فتزيدها سلبا او ايجابا قالت نظرية التحليل النفسي ان الغريزة الجنسية هي الجوهر والاصل والمسبب للمعرفة .
٣١) الفيلسوف في نظرية المعرفة يريد ان يفهم العالم والعارف يريد ان يصل الى كنه وحقيقة الوجود ويتصل به ويشاهده .
(٣٢) الادوات التي يستخدمها الفيلسوف في حركته العقل والمنطق والاستدلال في حين ان العارف يضيف لها القلب والتصفية والتهذيب.
24) The Quranic theory dealt with moral values as fixed axioms and mental postulates, while most philosophical theories dealt with moral values as accidental results of knowledge. 25) The Quranic theory spoke about the inheritance of negative and positive traits, such as the inheritance of the bad side (as in the case of the Children of Israel) and the inheritance of the positive side (as in the inheritance of the family of Yasin), while philosophical theories of knowledge did not pay attention to this aspect at all. 26) The Quranic theory stated that there are destructive and evil elements that affect the decision made by humans, namely the devils, while philosophical theories considered matters of good and evil as relative issues that change according to temporal and spatial conditions. 26) The Quranic theory stated in knowledge that insanity is the domination of devils over the soul, leading to the collapse of the system of insight, and philosophical theories did not address this topic at all. Philosophers neglected this important epistemological topic and referred it to psychology, which avoided its treatment or interpretation, and turned it back to psychiatry, which sufficed with palliative or anesthetic treatments. 27) Language in philosophical theories is formed through experience, training, and need, while in the Quranic theory its primary basic vocabulary is inspiration from God (And He taught Adam all the names) (He taught him expression). 28) The Holy Quran differed with philosophical theories on the subject of dreams. While the Quran said they are an important source of knowledge, philosophical theories said that dreams are psychological manifestations of no value, and some said that dreams are psychological disturbances. Descartes' acknowledgment of the role of dreams in inspiring him with analytical geometry must be recorded, but this acknowledgment was not intended as a sound methodological scientific indication that dreams are a source of knowledge, but rather as a recording of a strange and wondrous story, which does not give Descartes' acknowledgment any value. Rather, we record this dream as a point of defect in his thinking, not the opposite. 29) The Holy Quranic theory said that certain knowledge is possible for humans whose hearts are purified, their minds clear, and who perform spiritual exercises and psychic struggles, so the veils will be lifted from them and they will know the secrets of the universe and the world like one who sees in a mirror and sees what he needs or wants from the past, present, or future, while philosophical theories stopped at rational inferences and proofs. The Sufi theory can be excepted from this rule, though it differs from the Holy Quran in resources and purposes. 30) The Holy Quran differed with the theory of psychoanalysis in estimating the value of the sexual instinct. While the Quran said that this instinct has great importance in some decisions of the soul, increasing it negatively or positively, the theory of psychoanalysis said that the sexual instinct is the essence, origin, and cause of knowledge. 31) The philosopher in the theory of knowledge wants to understand the world, while the gnostic wants to reach the essence and reality of existence, connect with it, and witness it. 32) The tools used by the philosopher in his movement are intellect, logic, and inference, while the gnostic adds to them the heart, purification, and discipline.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a comparative enumeration by the author of ten points distinguishing the Quranic theory of knowledge from various philosophical theories. The author proceeds by stating each contrast directly. Point 24: The Quran treats moral values as fixed, axiomatic truths, whereas philosophy sees them as contingent byproducts of knowledge. Point 25: The Quran acknowledges hereditary transmission of both positive and negative traits (citing the Israelites and the family of Yasin), which philosophy ignores. Point 26 (first): The Quran affirms the existence of satanic influences on human decision-making, while philosophy relativizes good and evil to time and place. Point 26 (second): The Quran attributes insanity to demonic possession and collapse of insight, while philosophy relegates it to psychology and then to psychiatry, offering only palliative treatments. Point 27: Language, for philosophy, arises from experience, training, and need; for the Quran, it is divinely inspired, as in the verse 'And He taught Adam all the names' and 'He taught him expression.' Point 28: The Quran values dreams as a source of knowledge; philosophy dismisses them as valueless psychic phenomena. The author criticizes Descartes' acknowledgment of a dream inspiring his geometry as a mere curiosity, not a valid epistemological source. Point 29: Certain knowledge is attainable for those who purify heart and mind through spiritual discipline, leading to direct vision of past, present, and future; philosophy limits itself to rational proofs. The author notes an exception for Sufism but emphasizes its divergence from the Quran. Point 30: The Quran acknowledges the sexual instinct's influence on the soul positively or negatively; psychoanalysis treats it as the essence and origin of all knowledge. Point 31: The philosopher seeks to understand the world; the gnostic seeks to reach and witness the reality of existence. Point 32: The philosopher's tools are intellect, logic, and inference; the gnostic adds the heart, purification, and self-discipline.

Quranic Certainty: Beyond Rational Proofs
Author critiques philosophical rationalism via Quranic epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic conditions for certain knowledge (ma'rifa yaqiniyya) and contrast them with the philosophical reliance on rational deduction alone.

Core Idea
Certain knowledge requires heart purification, not just rational proofs.

This passage argues that Quranic epistemology offers a path to certainty through spiritual purification, going beyond the limits of rational philosophy. The author critiques philosophical rationalism for stopping at rational deductions, while the Quran promises unveiling for purified hearts. This lesson unpacks that contrast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic claim
Find where the author states that certain knowledge is possible for those whose hearts are purified and minds clear.
The key phrase is 'ma'rifa yaqiniyya'.
2
Extract the conditions
Note the three conditions: heart purification, spiritual exercises (riyadat), and lifting of veils (raf' al-hujub).
3
Contrast with philosophy
Observe the author's claim that philosophers stop at rational deductions and proofs (istidlalat wa barahin 'aqliyya).
This is the core of the critique.
4
Find the exception
The Sufi theory is excepted but differs in objectives and details.
5
Analyze the Descartes critique
Why does the author dismiss Descartes' dream? Because it was not a serious epistemological source but a strange anecdote.
This reinforces the author's view that non-Quranic spiritual experiences lack credibility.

ان الرؤيا عبارة عن اضطرابات نفسية ولابد من تسجيل اعتراف ديكارت بدور الرؤيا المنامية في الهامه علم الهندسة التحليلية ولكن هذا الاعتراف لم تكن غايته الاشارة العلمية المنهجية الرصينة بكون الرؤيا المنامية مصدرا للمعرفة بل كانت من باب تسجيل الحكاية الغريبة العجيبة مما لا يعطي لاعتراف ديكارت هذا اية قيمة بل نسجل هذه الرؤيا كنقطة خلل في تفكيره وليس العكس. ۲۹ ) قالت نظرية القرآن الكريم ان المعرفة اليقينية ممكنة للبشر ممن طهرت قلوبهم وصفت اذهانهم وقاموا بالرياضات الروحية والمجاهدات النفسية حيث سترتفع الحجب عن هؤلاء فيعرفون اسرار الكون والعالم كمن يرى في المرآة فيرى ما يحتاج او يريد من الماضي او الحاضر او المستقبل في حين وقفت نظريات الفلاسفة عند حدود الاستدلالات والبراهين العقلية. ويمكن استثناء النظرية الصوفية من هذه القاعدة مع اختلافها عن القرآن الكريم في الموارد والمقاصد. ۳۰ ) اختلف القرآن الكريم مع نظرية التحليل النفسي في تقدير قيمة الغريزة الجنسية ففي حين قال القرآن ان لهذه الغريزة اهمية بالغة في بعض قرارات النفس فتزيدها سلبا او ايجابا قالت نظرية التحليل النفسي ان الغريزة الجنسية هي الجوهر والاصل والمسبب للمعرفة. ۳۱) الفيلسوف في نظرية المعرفة يريد ان يفهم العالم والعارف يريد ان يصل الى كنه وحقيقة الوجود ويتصل به ويشاهده. (۳۲) الادوات التي يستخدمها الفيلسوف في حركته العقل والمنطق والاستدلال في حين ان العارف يضيف لها القلب والتصفية والتهذيب. ۳۳ ( قال القرآن الكريم بوجود ميزان في اعماق كل انسان يستطيع من خلاله ان يميز بين المتناقضات في دنيا الحياة في حين لاتوجد لدى الفلاسفة اية نظرة واضحة في هذا الجانب نتائج البحث ۱) ان ما يلاحظه الباحث في نظرية المعرفة في القرآن الكريم هو الغنى والتنوع والحيوية والشمولية وانفتاح النوافذ المعرفية الداخلية والخارجية الثابتة والمتحركة العواطف والمبادىء الاولية ليلا ونهارا. ۲) لابد من التنويه ان قوة الحجة القرآنية واصالة نظرية القرآن في المعرفة مصدرها الاول والاساس هو الاعجاز القرآني ۲ ) ان الفلاسفة اختلفوا في تعيين الادوات التي يكتسب بها الانسان معارفه وانقسموا على طوائف . الاولى جنحت الى الحس ورأوه الرصيد الاول والاساس للمعرفة وهؤلاء هم الحسيون والطائفة الثانية جنحت الى العقل ورأته الاداة الاهم لكسب المعارف وهؤلاء هم العقليون والثالثة رفضت الحس والعقل وركزت جل اهتمامها على الالهام والاشراق وهؤلاء هم الاشراقيون في حين نجد ان نظرية القرآن الكريم وازنت بين جميع مصادر المعرفة وآلياتها بدقة متناهية. ۴) ان الاصول التي يتبناها المادي في نظرته الكونية الى العالم تفرض عليه الا يعتقد الا بأداتين هما العقل والحس فهو لايرى الغيب والمعارف المفاضة الى قلوب الانبياء والعرفاء والاولياء وربما يخطؤه او يتغافلوا عنه اما القرآن الكريم فقد رأى ان دائرة الوجود اوسع من المادة وان هناك عالما غائبا عن حواسنا من الممكن ان نتصل به ونقف على اشياء لانقف عليها بالحس والعقل وان الفلسفات المادية قد بان عليها الفشل الذريع
Dreams are psychological disturbances, and it is necessary to record Descartes' acknowledgment of the role of the dream in inspiring him with analytic geometry. But this acknowledgment was not intended as a serious scientific methodological indication that the dream is a source of knowledge; rather, it was a recording of a strange and wondrous story, which gives no value to this acknowledgment of Descartes. Rather, we record this dream as a point of weakness in his thinking, not the opposite. 29) The Quranic theory stated that certain knowledge is possible for humans whose hearts are purified, whose minds are clear, and who undertake spiritual exercises and psychological struggles, for the veils will be lifted from them, and they will know the secrets of the universe and the world, like one who sees in a mirror, seeing what he needs or wants of the past, present, or future. Meanwhile, the theories of philosophers stopped at the limits of rational deductions and proofs. The Sufi theory can be excepted from this rule, albeit with its differences from the Quran in matters and objectives. 30) The Quran differed from the theory of psychoanalysis in assessing the value of the sexual instinct. While the Quran said that this instinct has great importance in some decisions of the self, increasing it positively or negatively, the theory of psychoanalysis said that the sexual instinct is the essence, origin, and cause of knowledge. 31) The philosopher in epistemology wants to understand the world, while the knower wants to reach the essence and reality of existence, connect with it, and witness it. (32) The tools that the philosopher uses in his movement are intellect, logic, and inference, while the knower adds to them the heart, purification, and refinement. 33) The Quran said that there is a scale in the depths of every human being through which he can distinguish between contradictions in the life of this world, whereas philosophers have no clear view in this regard. Results of the research: 1) What the researcher observes in the Quranic theory of knowledge is richness, diversity, vitality, comprehensiveness, and openness of internal and external cognitive windows, fixed and moving, emotions and primary principles, night and day. 2) It must be noted that the strength of the Quranic argument and the authenticity of the Quran's theory of knowledge have as their first and main source the Quranic inimitability (i'jaz). 3) The philosophers differed in determining the tools by which humans acquire their knowledge and divided into groups. The first inclined towards sense perception and saw it as the primary and fundamental basis of knowledge – these are the sensualists. The second group inclined towards reason and saw it as the most important tool for acquiring knowledge – these are the rationalists. The third rejected sense and reason and focused their attention on inspiration and illumination – these are the illuminationists. Meanwhile, we find that the Quranic theory balanced all sources of knowledge and their mechanisms with extreme precision. 4) The principles that the materialist adopts in his worldview force him to believe only in two tools: reason and sense. So he does not see the unseen and the knowledge poured into the hearts of prophets, gnostics, and saints, and perhaps he errs or ignores them. But the Quran has seen that the circle of existence is broader than matter, and that there is a world absent from our senses that we can connect with and come to know things that we cannot know through sense and reason, and that materialist philosophies have suffered utter failure.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a critical comparison between the Quranic theory of knowledge and various philosophical and psychological theories. The author begins by dismissing Descartes' dream as a mere anecdote, not a valid epistemological source. Then, point 29 asserts that the Quran allows certain (yaqini) knowledge through purification of the heart and spiritual exercises, unlike philosophers who rely solely on rational proofs. The Sufi theory is noted as an exception but differs from the Quran in specific details and goals. Point 30 contrasts the Quran's view of the sexual instinct as having important but limited influence on the soul with psychoanalysis, which makes it the essence and origin of knowledge. Point 31 distinguishes the philosopher's aim (understanding the world) from the 'arif's aim (reaching the essence of existence and witnessing it). Point 32 lists the tools: the philosopher uses intellect and logic; the knower adds heart and purification. Point 33 claims the Quran posits an innate scale (mizan) in humans to distinguish contradictions, while philosophers lack this. The 'Results of the research' summarize the superiority of the Quranic epistemology: its comprehensiveness (result 1), its foundation in i'jaz (result 2), its balanced approach compared to the three schools (sensualists, rationalists, illuminationists) (result 3), and its inclusion of the unseen world beyond matter, in contrast to failed materialism (result 4). The author uses Quranic epistemology as a standard to critique philosophical limitations.
